Julian 08 Sep 2015, 07:55

Cactus: you speculated last month about why, in the world of Harry Potter, anyone needs to wear glasses when you'd think eyesight could be corrected by magic. I've thought about this on and off ever since; but I think the real reason is that Joanne Rowling herself is quite myopic and wanted to provide spexy kids with a spexy hero as a role model. It occurs to me that on two occasions Harry's glasses were *repaired* by magic, the first time by Hermione on the train before they ever got to Hogwarts; and there are quite a few characters in the series who wear glasses - see http://harrypotter.wikia.com/wiki/Glasses. No mention anywhere of Harry or anyone else getting new glasses, or of an optical store in Diagon Alley.

Cactus Jack 16 Aug 2015, 14:11

I think most TV and Movie Directors and Producers have discovered, by now, that glasses with flat or "window glass" lenses are pretty obvious and detract from the story if the glasses are important (e.g. Harry Potter). I suspect, originally, they preferred them even for actors that actually wore glasses because of the ability to more easily control reflections from the powerful lights by carefully planning the camera angles.

The actual power in glasses lenses is determined by the difference between the curvature of the front and back surfaces of the glasses and the Index of refraction. You can have a Plano lens if the curvature is the same for both front and back. Also, these days, some of the AR coatings are almost invisible and reflection free . About the only way you can get an idea of a prescription, in a photograph, is to be able to see something in the background, through the lens, or be able to see the edge of the face through the lens and around the lens and look for "cut in" (-) or "cut out" (+).

One thing I never could understand about the Harry Potter stories was why, with all the magical tools that were available, Harry or anyone else, for that matter, needed glasses. A quick flick of the wand or a few sips of a magic potion and Voila!, perfect vision.

C.

Last week on a Match Game '79 episode broadcast on the Game Show Network, regular panelist Charles Nelson Reilly, who wore very large brown plastic frames, switched glasses with Daryl Anderson (Dennis "Animal" Price of "Lou Grant" fame), who wore small metal frames, before the start of the broadcast. He's famous for always wearing tinted glasses.

But now Johnny Depp has revealed the real reason for the accessory, admitting he is 'basically blind as a bat' in his left eye. 

The 50-year-old actor told Rolling Stone magazine that he has been suffering from eyesight issues from birth, and is forced to rely heavily on his prescription glasses.

In addition, Johnny said that he is near-sighted in his right eye, and neither condition can be treated.

He explained: 'Everything is just very, very blurry. I've never had proper vision.'

And while the actor is able to rely in his glasses in his personal life, when it comes to his film roles it's more difficult.

ksnl 27 Jun 2014, 10:55

Cactus Jack, I agree 100%, that's exactly what I was trying to say in my initial post. You cannot tell what someone's RX is... it's still fun to try and guess...

Cactus Jack 27 Jun 2014, 09:43

ksnl,

Look carefully at the guy with the -10.25 in the Right eye. You can just see the edge of his face through the lens. Notice the distance between the real edge and the edge as seen through the lens in his glasses.

Amount of cut in is NOT an accurate way to estimate Rx. There are too many factors that can affect apparent cut in. Rx is the main one, but Vertex Distance, Prism and viewing angle are also factors. Even a little prism or a small turn of the head can make a big difference in apparent cut in.

IMHO there is NO reliable way to guess a prescription. Guessing the number of beans in a jar is more productive. At least there, you typically have a chance of winning a prize.

C.

Cactus Jack 27 Jun 2014, 03:47

Power rings are caused by internal reflections of the edges of the lenses. If the edges of the lenses are thinner, the power rings will be less apparent.

The cut-in is almost the same in lower set of pictures. Compare the images of the Left Eye (right side in the pictures). Note the distance from the edge of the face outside the lens to the edge of the face as seen through the lens, They are almost the same distance with both pairs of glasses. It does not appear that there is any significant difference.

C.

ksnl 25 Jun 2014, 02:55

So I've come to the conclusion that we can't actually tell what someone's RX is unless the individual were to tell everyone what it is.

There are so many things that determine the amount of cut-in and power rings. For example, the width of the frame can make the RX appear higher (more cut-in, etc), also, if they are high index lenses, the RX appears to be much lower, you also have to take into account the angles, etc... http://www.smartopticals.com/images/High-Index%20Lenses.jpg

This guy apparently has an RX of -10.25 Right/-8.50 Left... http://spexyandheknowsit.tumblr.com/image/47780595482

Here is Kit Harington, it almost looks like he has more power rings than the above guy... http://kitharington.com/gallery/displayimage.php?pid=10269&fullsize;=1

Now I don't think Kit has that an RX anywhere that high but looks can be deceiving. Another thing to take into consideration is the fact that most celebrities, I'm sure, have high index lenses, so perhaps their RX is higher than we think?

Anyway, I just felt like divulging my thoughts. What do the rest of you think?

John S 18 Jun 2014, 00:19

richeye,

I don't know where you have gathered your information. A lot of people under 40(especially kids)are prescribed slightly more plus for their distance rx in an attempt to cause their muscles to fully relax. Have you not noticed a kid looking over the top of their plus lenses? He/she is doing that to get rid of the distance blur.

If what you say is true, please explain why starting at age 13, I needed a +1.00 for distance, and additional +2.00 for reading. I can assure you that I could not see distance through the +3.00 lenses, and I could not see close things without great difficulty through the +1.00 lenses.

At age 58, I still have almost the same rx, except for a strong add which I prefer for working with electronics.

I suggest you research the term accommodative insufficiency, and the types of other accommodative disorders.

Your posting reminds of of the first time I went to get glasses. The doctor said I only needed a +1.00 for distance. I didn't need a reading prescription, even though I could not see the reading chart. It appears you think the same way.

richeye 17 Jun 2014, 09:32

cactus jack

I totally agree, you may need "reading glasses" in younger years, too. Only difference: wearing those + rx glasses doesn't make the vision of more distant things blurred.

Especially farsighted children often get lower prescription than they actually need, just to keep their eyes flexible. Or they don't wear their glasses all day but for reading...(I was one of those kids myself...)

KL 14 Jun 2014, 21:36

Cactus Jack - thank you for taking the time to experiment and explain! The 2x focal distance actually makes a lot more sense.

Cactus Jack 14 Jun 2014, 21:00

KL,

I may not have been right about the inversion thing. Plus lenses will invert images. To get a better handle on the phenomenon, I used a +5.00 lens and a tape measure to do a crude experiment.

With my glasses on, looking though the distance segment, the +5.00 lens made a distant object (a wall clock about 4 meters away) very blurry when I held the lens next to the lenses in my glasses. Objects at 20 cm were clear as would be expected. As I moved the lens away from my eyes the blurry image got larger until the +5.00 lens was about 20 cm away from my eyes. The focal distance of a +5.00 lens is 20 cm.

As I moved the lens beyond 20 cm, the distant image became "confused" and as I moved the lens to 40 cm. (2X the focal distance) the inverted image began to resolve itself into an inverted image. As I moved the +5 lens even farther away, the inverted image came into shaper focus and degreased in apparent size.

As a second test, i held the +5 lens at about 40 cm (2X the focal distance) where the distant image had begun to clear, but was inverted. I then moved closer to the distant object. closer, As I approached the clock, the image became confused and then inverted back to normal orientation. The image was large and a little fuzzy. As I got closer the image became a bit smaller and sharper. The +5.00 lens had begun to act like a typical magnifying glass.

After all that, I think Julian is right about the hyperopia/presbyopia. I would guess maybe a +3 where part of that is correcting his hyperopia and he perhaps has enough accommodation left to need some help reading, but not more than +1 or +1.50 for a total of +3.00 in reading glasses. If this were the case, if he looked up with his reading glasses still on, his vision would be like an uncorrected myope who needs -1.50 glasses. Not sharp, but not impossible to function either.

The important point is this. What you see when looking through + glasses being worn by someone else, depends on your distance from the lenses AND the distance of the objects you see through the lens.

I knew there was some reason I did not like to play "Guess the Prescription" and now I understand why.

C.

Why do you say that? The picture you linked to (who was posted by a fellow "Optic Obsessive") shows Jake's contacts, not any evidence of surgery. As far as the eye that he is nearly blind in, it may be amblyopia. Either srabismus or a big difference in refraction can cause the brain to use the stronger eye and the visual pathway in the brain does not develop properly in the other eye. Cactus Jack can probably explain it better than I can.

asdoo and astigmaphile: "Scriptfinder" has been bandied about on this site from time to time, but there's no good reason for the existence of a database of celebrities real/accurate prescriptions, as these are personal data held by medical professionals.

Filthy McNasty 06 Jun 2011, 11:15

Of interest. Note that the writer has mischaracterized the character's refreactive error as myopia:

"LORD OF THE RINGS star ELIJAH WOOD had to don such thick glasses for his role in new film EVERYTHING IS ILLUMINATED, he was forced to wear reverse strength contact lenses so he could actually see.

Wood, who is himself shortsighted, had to play a character with an even more severe case of myopia, and his central costume piece caused a lot more problems than he'd anticipated.

He says, "We had to figure it out because they were +7 lenses, so they were magnified to the point where looking through it,everything was a massive fish bowl and I couldn't see.

"And I'm actually relatively blind myself. So, we had to get contact lenses that were -10 to offset the balance so that I could actually see. And I could see relatively well.

"But there were a couple of days where we didn't get the contacts properly sorted out and that was kind of complex.""

Cactus Jack 19 Apr 2011, 12:00

Myopic Grant,

LEGALLY BLIND is defined by LAW to determine eligibility for government aid or assistance. It is really not applicable in this instance, but it sounds dramatic for the TV audience.

Legally Blind means that a person's best CORRECTED vision in one eye is 20/200 or worse or has a visual field of 20 degrees or less instead of the usual 180 degrees. In other words, there is just no known way to improve it.

My first Rx was -1.50 in one eye and Plano in the other. I could not make out the big E (20/200) line with the -1.50 eye without correction. With correction my vision was better than 20/20 so I was not "Legally Blind" in that eye or "Legally Blind" at all. A person could need -20 myodiscs and they corrected him to better than 20/200 he would not be Legally Blind". Because very high plus glasses can have very limited fields of vision, it is possible that while a person can see better than 20/200 straight ahead with correction, it is possible that they are "Legally Blind" because their field of vision is less than 20 degrees.

Jimmy Fallon could be "Legally Blind" if he could not be corrected. Obviously, he can be corrected - probably with glasses, contacts, or Lasik- so he was not and is not LEGALLY BLIND.

The key point is the person can't see better than 20/200 WITH the best possible correction. 20/200 can occur without as low as -1.50 so it really depends on the visual acuity after correction.

C.

ksnl 06 Apr 2011, 15:26

I think Jake Gyllenhaal has Keratoconus... I saw that he has intacs inserted into his corneas in this pic: http://www.flickr.com/photos/31161629@N06/3612088008/in/set-72157619425294005/ posted on here a while back. I know what this looks like because my cousin, aunt and a friend's dad have all had this done for keratoconus. It's when the cornea keeps changing shape or something... I know that if you have keratoconus your rx keeps changing so they usually opt for contacts, the reason he would never be seen in glasses. The corneal intact surgery would improve eyesight but not make it anywhere near perfect, he would still need correction. Like my cousin who has had the operation and still has poor eyesight. Keratonus varies in severity from person to person. Here's info on it and pics of intacs: http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keratoconus

"Scriptfinders" does not exist. In order to find out prescription information, one would have to obtain it from the Optometrist, and that would be a complete HIPPA violation which would lead to the loss of their licence. Guessing one's prescription is one thing, but let's not lie about having this information anymore.

Extract from an interview with Daniel Radcliffe:

Do you wear glasses when you're not playing Harry Potter?

I'm supposed to but I always lose them or a lens falls out or something. So after we went through three pairs, we stopped buying them. I even managed to break my Harry Potter glasses at one stage. But there were a lot of pairs, a whole row of them in the prop department.

Wayne 14 Mar 2008, 21:01

There is significant cut-in showing in the picture of Justin Bartha. Trying to estimate Rx from the cut-in can be complicated. Cut-in is a combination of the strength of the Rx, the size of the frames and of the face, the angle at which the head is turned and the distance of the lenses from the eyes.

I can make pretty good estimates if the lenses are mostly minus -- without a lot of cylinder or especially prism. In the case of Bartha, I'd estimate at least -5 or -6, possibly more.

I base this on the amount of visible cut-in with the head only slightly turned (and frames that aren't excessive large or small) combined with the apparent minification of his eyes in proportion to his face and the minification of objects behind him as seen through his left lens.

Note how tiny and moved over the white pillar looks as seen through his left lens. Also the top of his ear as seen through the lens is so small you can't really see it. The angle of the pillar through the lens makes me suspect some cylinder for astigmatism.

Technical details aside, he looks really sexy in those glasses. I'd love to have him take them off and then lean close to see see me with his big, bare brown eyes.

All4Eyes 25 Jan 2008, 15:09

This isn't really about an actor so much as some interesting conversation I heard on an episode of "A Different World" (sitcom from the 80's or 90's I guess, in reruns. I've never watched it before, but this got my attention). This girl Whitney had a hot dream about this guy Dwayne, who wears round metal glasses with sunglass clip-ons (as with most glasses on TV characters, I couldn't discern much, if any, rx). She was talking about it to her friend, who collapsed into laughter and said "I just want to know one thing: Did he have his glasses on? Did they get steamed up?" (yes, technically that's 2 things, but anyway...). She said it laughing, like what a joke it was that Whitney found this four-eyed guy hot, but for someone like Us (like me), mmmm, what a great picture! Then later Whitney is describing her dream to someone else, but tries to avoid naming names: "My companion and I wear floating along a stream in a canoe, when suddenly the stream turned into a raging river! The boat started rocking so hard that Dwayne's glasses, uh, I mean my companion's glasses, flew off!" Then she went on about how they were "tossing back and forth and back and forth... And I've never "canoed" before, but despite my inexperience, I found myself "paddling" with passion and gusto, over and over and over...!" Yeah, I know the feeling, Whit. Anyway, I though that was cool.

I ALWAYS make passes at (and occasionally dream about) guys who wear glasses, Marie

Jon 12 Nov 2007, 08:52

Having read a preview of 'My Boy Jack', Julian, I watched it last night too.

I suppose it was inevitable that it had both Jack (Daniel Radcliffe) and his father Rudyard depicted wearing plano lenses, despite both of them being notoriously nearsighted.

There were however, some interesting dialogue and scenes where Jack's eyesight and glasses were the primary theme. It's not too often that is the situation on television or the movies.

It's a pity the drama didn't go into the heartache that his, and indeed many families through many conflicts have felt through not knowing his resting place. Apparently this was not discovered until 1992. Even then it was argued by certain historians that it was the burial place of another lieutenant from Kiplings' regiment who went 'missing' two days before Jack.

Julian 12 Nov 2007, 08:13

After 'Learners' I switched channels and watched part of 'My boy Jack' about Rudyard Kipling's son who was killed at the battle of Loos in 1915. Apparently the lad was so short-sighted that he was turned down by both the army and the navy and only allowed to enlist because his father used his influence. He is played by the lovely Daniel Radcliffe, who at 18 is just the same age as Jack when he died. With a certain inevitability, the glasses he wears are plano (gold ovals).

Odd how many times Daniel gets parts that require him to wear glasses...there's a shot of him among the Google images in Scout uniform and round glasses, not unlike the Harry Potter ones but not identical.

I found an interesting passage in this book: http://www.amazon.co.uk/Doctor-Who-Inside-Story-Official/dp/056348649X/ref=pd_bbs_sr_1/202-7893259-1610243?ie=UTF8&s;=books&qid;=1184622072&sr;=8-1 It's from a section where they are talking about how they decided on David Tennant's costume as the tenth doctor.

""The glasses," says David, "were one of thos things that just kind of arose. As we put together the look, it was becoming this sort of geek-chic thing, it seemed to make sense to add a pair of specs to that. There was one point where I was thinking about having them on all the time, but that got a bit of resistance from some people, and maybe they were right; I don't know. I quite like the idea of there being a speccy hero, I mean it certainly hasn't done Harry Potter any harm. And maybe because I grew up "speccy four eyes" in school, I would have quite liked to have had support from the Doctor on that. It just seemed right.""

Cleo 30 Jan 2007, 15:14

I found this article:

Short-sighted actor JAMES SPADER spends his days in a blur - because the writers on hit legal drama THE PRACTICE don't like his character wearing glasses.

The SECRETARY star wore his spectacles when he made his debut as ALAN SHORE in The Practice earlier this year (03), but producers hated his look.

Spader says, "In the first episode I wore glasses and I thought, 'Great, I'm going to be able to see,' because my eyes don't tolerate contact lenses.

"If I can get a character to wear glasses, I like it. I said, 'Wouldn't it be great if he wore glasses, because it would be nice if I could actually see during the course of the filming.'

"I thought it was fine but they said, 'No with the glasses,' so now all day everything's a complete blur. At the end of the day I have a headache.

"Then I'll put on the glasses in between the set ups, so, if you look very closely at my scenes in close up, there'll be two marks (on my nose)."

Interview with the very sexy Chris Pine (Just my Luck; Princess Diaries 2) about why his character wore glasses in one scene in the Princess Diaries and how he had to learn to act with out seeing:

http://movies.about.com/library/weekly/aapd2cb080804b.htm

From another site: http://www.manilatimes.net/national/2004/aug/24/yehey/enter/20040824ent2.html

Chris and I have had so much fun on this film, says Anne Hathaway. Weve had some amazing scenes together in which Im brimming over with passion for my fellow actor, making what I thought was great eye contact with him from across the room, my hearts fluttering, then at the end of the take, Id say Wasnt that good?! And he hadnt seen me the entire timehes blind as a bat!

Chris Pine is a wonderful actor, but he doesnt see very well, adds director Gary Marshall. Chris wears glasses, and when he takes the glasses off hes very dashing, but he cant see where everything is. So I did one scene where his character wears glasses, and Chris was so happy in this scene because he could see everybody and he knew what was going on!

Gregory 25 Feb 2006, 12:34

Matthew Perry discusses his glasses in an encounter with a fan. He hints that he is both myopic and astigmatic:

That's right, I met Matthew Perry. He said my name three times. I'm sorry, what? You didn't catch that?

Matthew Perry said my name THREE TIMES.

Pam and her man took me out to a burlesque show for the birthday of one of their friends, and we weren't there ten minutes when Matthew (I just call him Matthew) walked in. Also in attendance: Julie Benz of Buffy, Angel, and Roswell (I didn't know about that one, but Djb filled me in, and if you think Pam is cool, wait until you meet him) fame, who was very nice when I gushed all over her about how much I loved Darla; Hank Azaria, who was the recipient of a patented Chandler Bing triple-take when the pretty lady was shaking her ass on stage; and the parking lot guy from Ferris Bueller. Quite the Hollywood random sampling, no?

Anyway, so let's talk about my boyfriend. I had been trying to sidle up to him when Pam saw he was going to smoke, and pushed me out the door, "Go smoke! Go talk to him! Go!" Who was I to argue with Miss L.A. 2002? I went.

I didn't talk to him immediately, but we moved close enough to his ass to be within hearing distance of his conversation, and check this shit out: When I commented to Pam that I wanted to buy the strippers new tights, guess who laughed at my joke?

Matthew Perry.

About thirteen cigarettes and six drinks later, I saw my opportunity to strike. Here is what I said:

AB: So, I've been stalking you all night and I just thought you might like to know.

Matthew: Really? Well, it is good to know. Nice to meet you.

AB: Nice to meet you. I'm Anna Beth.

Matthew: Anna Belle?

AB: No, Anna Beth.

Matthew: Ah, Anna Beth. (there's one.) This is my [agent, lawyer, somebody. I don't care.].

AB: [to guy] Nice to meet you! I like your glasses.

Matthew: We all have glasses. They're good for seeing. Are you nearsighted, Anna Beth? (Two.)

AB: Yes, I am!

Matthew: Astigmatism?

AB: Nope.

Matthew: D'oh! Well, it was nice to meet you, Anna Beth. (And, three.) Enjoy your trip to L.A.!

Would I lie to y'all? Right about now Allison is shaking her fists at the sky because she was supposed to come on this trip and couldn't. Hey, Al? Remember that time you went to L.A. and saw Daisy Fuentes in a wig shop? I win!

This is getting really long, so I'm going to have to ask you to click "next" to read Part II. Well, go on!

I used to wear glasses for far-sightedness for a couple of years from the ages of about 9 to 11, and now I'm short-sighted!

Furtive 04 Dec 2005, 12:34

Yes, I think it's possible for a hyperopic child to eventually "outgrow" the condition and end up myopic. But it is also possible for the child to outgrow their need for glasses but remain hyperopic, in which case they end up needing glasses again at some point as adults.

I knew a couple of kids who wore thick plus glasses as little kids but then were told they didn't need glasses anymore - or needed them only for reading - when they were 13 or so. I think there's some threshold of hyperopia for which glasses are usually prescribed for young children in order to prevent strabismus, or amblyopia if the eyes are very different, but when the kids are older these aren't really risks anymore, so if the kid has decent acuity then glasses aren't needed at that point.

Wayne 04 Dec 2005, 10:27

I believe that I've heard that hyperopia in a young child can decrease over time to where they need weaker glasses or even no glasses.

It would make sense as it would be the same as the progression of myopia -- the eyeball grows (or stretches?) longer. For myopes their eyesight gets worse, but hyperopes eyesight would get better.

I suppose that would mean one could start out hyperopic as a young child and end up myopic as one gets older.

Julian 25 Nov 2005, 10:14

Interesting, this business of kids who cease to be hyperopic. Do they just have a longer way to go on the slippery slope to myopia? Any experts comment? (I know it's off topic for this thread, but it follows on logically, to me anyhow.)

I've seen some shows about the making of the Harry Potter movies and in them the actor has stated that there are multiple pairs of glasses - some have no lenses at all in fact - and that it depends on what sort of reflection they want to get, or whether they want no reflection at all.

There are a number of magazine articles and such in which Radcliffe has been asked whether he wears glasses in real life. In the oldest ones he stated that he had glasses that he rarely wore - and the stories that came out when he was first chosen for the role often reported that he wore glasses, just like his character. In one case he said that he was supposed to wear glasses for reading, but didn't usually wear them. However, when he's been asked about this more recently (during the time of the release of the last two movies) he has stated that he used to wear glasses but doesn't need them anymore. This sounds as though he might be one of those farsighted children who outgrows the need for glasses (at least temporarily) as he ages.

Julian 27 Oct 2005, 03:48

Here's an extract from an interview with Carmine Giovinazzo:

CSI Files: Fans have taken note of Danny's new glasses, which he didn't wear in the CSI: Miami episode ("MIA/NYC--NonStop") that introduced the NY cast. Why the change?

Giovinazzo: That was part of the character. We're creating a character and I think [the addition of the glasses] worked out for the best. They might come off at some point. I've kind of gotten used to them. Once [I] put those on, you know who this guy is. It's not me, although I do wear glasses.

CSI Files: Did that have anything do with the addition of the glasses?

Giovinazzo: No, no, it was completely a decision that was made as we were beginning to do the show. [Though i]f I took them off, I couldn't see things. I'm blind without them.

CSI Files: It sounds like it was a good addition then.

Giovinazzo: It's nice. I don't have to do [the show] with my contacts on all the time. I can let my eyes breathe.

-oo- 07 Mar 2005, 09:10

I vote for astigmatism - in fact thats what I always thought. Also, as I recall from my youth, it seemed like there were people who wore what looked like weak minus glasses all thru school, and then meeting up with them a few years after college, they would be wearing plus. I wonder if it was the custom back in the 60 & 70s not to prescribe the plus part of the prescrption for young hyperopic astigmats without diplopia (eye crossing) in an effort to allow as much emmitropisation (allowing the eye to grow out of hyperopia) as possible.

See - I was noticing this stuff even then!

Here's an interesting quote re: Johnny Depp:

"Acting is very easy for Johnny. You never see him rehearse his lines. He comes to the set very relaxed and fulfills his task. This was very stimulating. He was interested in old books in any case. He read some of them before the shooting. After that he just put on his costume. I asked him all the time: 'What do you think of this? If you think it's good, I think that too,' was his laconic reply. Concerning his glasses, I explained to him that I wanted him to wear real glasses, because they give a person a different kind of look in the eyes. When he tried them on, he screamed that they made him blind. I insisted on him playing the role like that. Luckily he accepted and for the whole movie he wore glasses through which he actually saw nothing." - Roman Polanski

Julian 04 Mar 2005, 05:57

deppendent: I'm not entirely convinced by all you say about Johnny's eyesight. Your marshal your arguments well, but they aren't conclusive.

1. He wore glasses a a kid...if they were for myopia I'd expect obvious cut-in and power rings by now.

2. In my experience lots of people use 'near-sighted' as a generic term for not seeing well. (I remember one friend of mine saying, "Sorry, I can't read that; I'm short-sightedwell actually I'm long-sighted.")

3. The glasses he wears in 'The Ninth Gate' are unmistakeably minus - but show me another picture of him where the lenses reveal that...if Roman Polanski wanted a myopic character perhaps he did GOC.

4. In the shots I have of the 2004 BAFTAs his lenses look low plus to me. And in the shots I've seen from 'The Secret Window' they alos looked plus.

5. I'm a low hyperope with slight astigmatism - and I'll bet I couldn't read a teleprompter bareyed.

I think the jury is still out.

deppendent 03 Mar 2005, 22:02

My long time obsession is Johnny Depp, and Electra you have it wrong, Johnny is definitely nearsighted by his own admission. In a 2003 interview with Italian Vanity Fair he responded to whats with the glasses, are you nearsighted? with just a bit. Since you seem to have developed a crush on our boy heres some trivia for you.

1986 Platoon. A yet-to-be famous Johnny appears in all of the on-set publicity pictures wearing glasses.

1987-1990 21 Jump Street. Johnny wore his glasses in many of the episodes as an undercover disguise for his cop character.

1993 What Eating Gilbert Grape. Stories from the rural Texas location where the movie was shot was that Johnny would sneak off the set to hit the music clubs in Austin incognito in glasses, of course.

1994 Oscars. Johnny and others often recount this famous story about his experience as an Oscar presenter. Johnny showed up for rehearsal and discovered that the teleprompter was too far away for him to read the copy. Instead of wearing his glasses, he asked the writers to shorten his introduction to a few words. Shortly after the Oscars incident, he started wearing contact lenses on and off the set, and seemed to remain a happy wearer for several years.

1998 The Ninth Gate thats an interesting one. Electra, I dont know where you read the glasses were a prop Polanski made Johnny wear for realism. Polanski did talk about liking Johnny in glasses because they fit the character and helped age him. But I cant imagine a director compromising a performance by asking an actor who needs prescription glasses to wear prescription glasses, just not his own, and not in one scene, but the whole movie. I also cant image studio execs allowing a star who effectively cant see risk injury by running down steps in the dark and driving a speeding car. Shutting down production, even for a day, would have cost many thousands of dollars. I think the specs were the real deal.

2003. Johnny turns 40 and starts wearing glasses off-set again. Coincidence? I think not. When youre nearsighted, correcting distance vision starts messing up your close vision in your late thirties. If you want to see both near and far, your options start to suck. I think thats whats going on with him.

I started watching "CSI: NY" the new show with the recently discussed Gary Sinise. His costar, Carmine Giovinazzo wears glasses as "Danny". I found a blurb about it in an interview he did. They're a real prescription for once.

David

CSI Files: Fans have taken note of Danny's new glasses, which he didn't wear in the CSI: Miami episode ("MIA/NYC--NonStop") that introduced the NY cast. Why the change?

Giovinazzo: That was part of the character. We're creating a character and I think [the addition of the glasses] worked out for the best. They might come off at some point. I've kind of gotten used to them. Once [I] put those on, you know who this guy is. It's not me, although I do wear glasses.

CSI Files: Did that have anything do with the addition of the glasses?

Giovinazzo: No, no, it was completely a decision that was made as we were beginning to do the show. [Though i]f I took them off, I couldn't see things. I'm blind without them.

CSI Files: It sounds like it was a good addition then.

Giovinazzo: It's nice. I don't have to do [the show] with my contacts on all the time. I can let my eyes breathe.

An Actor 13 Aug 2004, 08:40

I'm one of the names mentioned way down in the thread and if it's OK with everyone here I'd like to speak up for those of us who don't always have the final say in how we look.

When you make your living dressing up as other people you have to do what the director and wardrobe people tell you to do. Sometimes that includes wearing glasses. For technical reasons usually they want you to wear prop glasses they have control over. Sometimes they let you wear your own glasses. Depends on time, budget, and other issues. But it's not unusual for an actor who has arrived on set in contacts to be told to wear prop glasses. We don't get a choice usually. Only the big names like Depp get to do that.

But thanks for noticing.

Furtive 06 Jun 2004, 19:17

I saw a TV show about the making of the Harry Potter movies. It had interviews with the cast, including Daniel Radcliffe. He showed the interviewer that the particular set of Harry Potter frames that he was wearing in the interview actually had no lenses in them at all (he stuck his finger through them to demonstrate.) He said that there are multiple pair of glasses and that the lense-less ones are used whenever the glare of the lights would be a problem, whereas those with lenses are used for close-ups in which it would be more apparent if there were no lenses.

D-W-V 07 Jan 2004, 21:11

Either a DVDROM or DVDRW will still function fine for CDROMs or audio CDs, so you don't need to keep your current CDROM drive. If you have a CD writer, most DVD writers also write CDRs and CDRWs.

D-W-V 07 Jan 2004, 21:07

DVDROM drives can be under $40 U.S.: http://www.tigerdirect.com/applications/category/category_slc.asp?CatId=88

I'd choose one that included a legit copy of WinDVD or PowerDVD, since those programs sell for around $40 separately. It might be wise to spend more and get a DVD+/-RW writer instead, now that they're into the $100 range. I'd lean towards getting one that supported both the + and - formats for maximum compatibility. http://www.tigerdirect.com/applications/Category/category_tlc.asp?CatId=4

http://www.newegg.com is another reputable vendor.

Electra 07 Jan 2004, 20:00

D-W-V 07 Jan 2004, 18:16

Electra:

The easiest way to do screen captures is to play the DVD on your computer (if you have a DVD drive); most playback programs include the ability to grab a screenshot. Using WinDVD, for example, hitting the "P" key will save a bmp of the screen.

'Bluespecs' says it's OK to post here what he posted in 'guysglasses 2' about actors in specs, so here goes:

Hi,

here are some movies with myope main actors wearing real glasses

- Rob Lowe in "Illegally Yours" (rectangle plastic frame, about 2,5 RX) nice scene when Rob Lowe gets in rain and is totally wet, his glasses still upon his nose

- James Spader in "Bad Influence" (round gold metal frame, about 2 RX) good scene when he fights with Rob Lowe and James' real glasses are falling down (watch this scene in slow-motion, it's great!)

- James Spader in "Stargate" (a different round gold metal frame, about 2 RX)

- Jeremy London in "Innocent Babysitter" (round black metal frame, about 3 RX)

- Lorenzo Lamas in "Back To Even" (also known as "The Debt") (2 different round gold metal frames, about 7 RX)

- Barry Miller in "The Chosen" (round plastic frame, about 5 RX) good scene when he gets hit in the eye by a baseball caused by Robby Benson and Barry Millers glasses break to pieces

- Robby Benson in "Jeremy" (black plastic frames) - good scene at the beginning of the movie when Jeremy wakes up without his glasses and puts them on

3 Pics of "Jeremy" I put in the new album actors.

If anybody knows other movies where actors do wear their real glasses, let us know.

Wish you a lot of fun and excitement by watching one or more of these movies.

bluespecs

I read an interview awhile back - I can't remember which actor - in which the actor talked about having difficulty with contacts and glasses in a movie that he was in. He stated that he had to wear contacts to "offset" his vision because in real life he has perfect vision but it was very important to the director that he wear real glasses and that he USE the glasses in the movie. So: at least in some cases, just because you see prescription glasses onscreen doesn't mean the actor wears glasses.

Christy 26 Dec 2002, 04:55

It's ages since I've seen Jaws - but they decided to dust off the old movie and show it on Christmas Day. I'd quite forgotten how well glasses featured in that movie. Two out of the three guys on the fishing boat Orca wore them - those guys also being the two surviving actors - the other one being eaten by the shark for Christmas dinner! Of course - they both lost their specs before the boat finally sank. They were real specs with appreciable distortion - and cunningly used in some takes. When one guy is reading up about sharks - the pages of the book are deliberately reflected in his glasses. Also - when he goes out to sea - his wife reminds him that she's packed a spare pair of glasses. Earlier than that - there's a woman whose son is eaten by the shark - and she's obviously quite myopic by the look of her glasses. Which all goes to show the moviemakers that there isn't really any excuse to be using planos and fake spex in qualtiy movies!

Julian 22 Feb 2002, 02:18

Kubla, you were asking what it all was about Elijah Wood. Well, he used to be a cute child actor and is now a very handsome young man of 21; so when somebody found a photo of him wearing glasses and reported it on the old Eye Scene BBS all the gay guys around the place went berserk (and the discussion got quite acrimonious). What is especially tantalizing (and titillating too!) is that as far as we can see he has only ever been photographed ONCE in specs. The debate raged about how strong they were, with suggestions from -1 to -5, but nobody at that time suggested they were plus. I have five different shots of him, all apparently taken on the same occasion (same clothes, same background) and I will shortly try to post them on Dominic's 'spexyguys' Yahoo group.

I think the people who think those are plus lenses are wrong. I think what we see in the pic that Guest points us (My No 1 when I post them) to is minification of the background. Also, in my No 2 I can see a bit of cut-in. Finally I think a comparison with a bare eyed pic (or rather one with contacts) will show that his eyes look smaller through his specs. Apologies to my fellow hyperopes, but I have looked long and lovingly at these photos <grin> and I don't think we can claim him as one of us. As Dom has mentioned, these photos are years old, and Kubla's report suggests his myopia has increased - "he's gotten so blind he even got bifocals for when he doesn't wear contacts". Bifocals are sometimes prescribed for young myopes to try and slow down the progress. I wish, and I'm not alone, that we could see some recent shots of him in his coke bottles.

Guest: I checked the first URL you gave us for Jeremy London and got a screenful of broken icons; but I think I know the pics you mean. To me it didn't look as if he was short sighted enough to justify LASIK. If anything can. Other actors you might have mentioned are James van der Beek, Brad Pitt and Freddie Prinze jr. Ryan Phillippe is sometimes seen in glasses too, but I suspect astigmatism rather than myopia.

Love and kisses, Jules.

dominic 18 Nov 2001, 16:08

At the risk of sounding arrogant (a risk I often take) I am pretty good at spotting Rxs from photos, films etc. I've been doing it obsessively for 25 years! Ryan's lenses in Antitrust have a mild prescription for astigmatism in the -.75 to -1.25 region; I would have said a plano base but I could be wrong. The angle of the cylinder is the same in both lenses. Those he wore in Cruel Intentions were pure plano - as are Daniel Radcliffe's all the way through the film. (Believe me, I kept a very careful look-out.) I suspect the minus glasses he wore for publicity shots had to be abandoned because they reflected the light. Quite often in films, an actor's prescription glasses get switched to non-reflective plano for close-ups.

Of course, the 21st century is derived from the Julian calendar 8-)

Thinking calendrically, the Mayan version is a worthy subject. Its 'welcome' of the Conquistadors as gods shows the folly of hewing to any specific interpretation of what a given time may represent. Yet it also indicates that there may be something to the ancient practice of prophecy.

Filthy McNasty 06 Nov 2001, 08:46

Interesting discussion about PCness. I suppose whether a given term is overly PC or simply courteous depends on your point of view, and on which end of the word in question you find yourself. To suggest that one's choice of words never matters would be silly. To hang on EVERY word is no less silly.

<p>

Some terms we now universally think of as racist or sexist were common usage not long ago. Popular language is inextricably intertwined with societal values; they evolve together and reflect each other. Terms we use to describe other people often carry a lot of information about whether that person or group of people is accepted as part of mainstream society or is relegated to the fringes.

<p>

I am with Wurm. Ultimately, it's courtesy that counts most.

Dru 06 Nov 2001, 07:29

Wurm 06 Nov 2001, 07:14

Julian,

Yes, I set up the Actresses thread first. I was trying to start threads that I could actually come up with content for!

I believe in encouraging courteous behavior in this forum, but I take a dim view of political correctness.

As I understand it, political correctness was a joke started by American lefties to poke fun at themselves. The concept of word police loose in America was intended to be very funny -- a simultaneous gloss on _1984_, McCarthyism and the intrinsic fragmentation of the Left -- but look where it led! Oh well, at least Bill Mahar got it.

Personally, I'm a freethinker. As long as we are having polite discussions, I don't care too much about the structure or topic. If it has something to do with glasses, so much the better.

Christy 06 Nov 2001, 00:26

The acting profession doesn't really subscribe to the usual ideals of sexism, racism or political correctness. The reason they don't is pretty obvious. If the movie plot calls for a white man, or a black woman, or a tall/short or fat/thin person - then those are the only people they're going to interview for the job. If a 'tall thin white man' didn't get a part in a movie when they were specifically looking for a 'short fat black woman' then there's little point him going to court over the matter - or vice versa!

Mind you - if the plot calls for a glasses-wearer - then wouldn't it be nice if they'd use a real glasses-wearer instead of someone in planos?
